  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_86017839-b63b-4a22-8cd8-d2e1a58fd1b7'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_133748090" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133748090" />
    <a title="Cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1876075-cara"><img alt="Cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350665534p2/1876075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133748090?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cara" href="/user/show/1876075-cara">Cara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=inspired-by-jane-austen">inspired-by-jane-austen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1876075-cara?shelf=gobblers">gobblers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133748090" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3036405493219779661">I am tempted to create a shelf called <i>the gobblers</i>. Gobblers are books that you soak up in one sitting and are usually oodles of fun. I used to be a gobbler fanatic. Picking up these types of books frequently and reading them like candy. I miss those days sometimes...<br/><br/>Anyways this particular story centers on Elise Benton. She's moved to a L.A. with her family and the changes of course are taking some time. Elise is going to a prep school where everyone knows a movie star, and her mother is the pr</span>
  <span id="freeText3036405493219779661" style="display:none">I am tempted to create a shelf called <i>the gobblers</i>. Gobblers are books that you soak up in one sitting and are usually oodles of fun. I used to be a gobbler fanatic. Picking up these types of books frequently and reading them like candy. I miss those days sometimes...<br /><br />Anyways this particular story centers on Elise Benton. She's moved to a L.A. with her family and the changes of course are taking some time. Elise is going to a prep school where everyone knows a movie star, and her mother is the principal. Ouch. There is one class in particular, Astronomy, that will be the most interesting. On the one hand in this class we have Derek Edwards, the brooding hunk with famous parents, and on the other we have Webster Grant, the easy-going guy with a fun attitude. Elise is a girl with a steady head on her shoulders and will not be wowed by the rich people environment, but there is just something about Derek. Grant says he’s trouble. Her sister Juliana is all doe-eyed with a boy named Chase, who happens to be best friends with Derek. What ensues are misunderstandings and misjudgments that create a big mess. A mess Elise is going to have to figure out.<br /><br />Overall the book was fun and sweet and it's not meant to be anything else than that really. There are some interesting tidbits like how Derek and his family deal with the fame. It even actually got me thinking of how annoying it would be and how much of a tough skin you'd have to develop having your every move monitored. I do think the book suffered a little though with the characters. Elise and her sister Juliana are great together, and the guys were cool too. Once we get to the Benton family, well not so cool. The younger sister Layla is plain annoying and the mom... well she was kind of dim. But I get it, in the original novel they weren't meant to be favorable characters either. The other characters do make up for it though, so I was content to just watch and see how the relationships turned out. The whole group of them: Elise, Derek, Juliana and Chase were <b>so cute</b>.<br /><br />What the author did well was make me believe this could be a story that carried itself and not need the layout of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a>. A reader can honestly pick up this book and have no prior knowledge of P&amp;P, but since I had read it I knew how things would turn out, so some of the fun was probably taken out of it because of that. <br /><br />I thought about saying nothing about the cover but alas I can't help myself. This cover is kind of misleading. The tagline epic fail doesn't play a prominent role at all and the holding of the notes isn't important either. About the only thing the cover depicts correctly is that there is in fact a guy and girl in the story. I guess the publishing house wanted to appeal to a teen audience, but I'm not a fan of the cover. Just sayin'<br /><br />All that aside though this is a wonderful light read, and I even giggled. I don't giggle very much, so I guess that means something right?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3036405493219779661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_268094466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268094466" />
    <a title="Maru" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7537410-maru"><img alt="Maru" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411788255p2/7537410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/268094466?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maru" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maru" href="/user/show/7537410-maru">Maru</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7537410-maru?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer268094466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer785658099474116488"><b>Rating: 1.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>The way I see it, Epic Fail was a pretty bad book with some ok moments. That's my overall reaction. Maybe it's not an EPIC fail, but it <i>is</i> somewhat of a fail nonetheless. It's just confusing, the characters are weird and flat, and - in my opinion - it's all quite boring. The majority <s>all</s> of the characters annoyed the hell out of me at one point or another, there a lot of stupid situations, and not many good developments of <i>anything</i>, but at least there are a few (keyword: few) fu</span>
  <span id="freeText785658099474116488" style="display:none"><b>Rating: 1.5 STARS</b><br /><br />The way I see it, Epic Fail was a pretty bad book with some ok moments. That's my overall reaction. Maybe it's not an EPIC fail, but it <i>is</i> somewhat of a fail nonetheless. It's just confusing, the characters are weird and flat, and - in my opinion - it's all quite boring. The majority <s>all</s> of the characters annoyed the hell out of me at one point or another, there a lot of stupid situations, and not many good developments of <i>anything</i>, but at least there are a few (keyword: few) fun moments in the end to make it an ok option when in the mood for a quick, light reading, that won't leave you with anything substantial. <br /><br />Elise Benton's family moves to Los Angeles after her mother gets a job as the principal of a private school there, school which Elise and her three other sisters will be attending. In this school there are many rich kids, famous kids, kids with famous parents, etc. One of them is Derek, son of the hottest couple in Hollywood. Elise notices how everyone seeks Derek's attention and she vows to not be <i>"that type of girl"</i>, befriending instead the 'loner' Webster. Staying away from Derek proves harder than it seems though when her sister Juliana starts dating Derek's best friend. <s>
  <i>Tun Tun Tun. Not</i>
</s><br /><br />The biggest problem I had with this book is that all the characters were morons, seriously. From the principal mother, to the younger sister, it's like they were all lacking serious social skills or something. They get better at the end, but for 3/4ths of the book, I didn't know which one I wanted to slap first. <br /><br /><b>Elise's</b> constant need to prove to everyone how different she is <s>not</s> from other girls in that she will not be following Derek around or giving him any special treatment because he's semi-famous is particularly irritating. Especially because in this quest to prove how much better she is than everyone else she ends up being the first one to judge, she's seriously hypocritical, and just the fact that she was so "proud of herself" for befriending Webster says it all. It's like the only reason she was befriending him was because he was a loner and this proved how much better she was than the rest of the school's population. Gaah, I wanted to yell at her to get off her high horse and get over herself. She never even gave Derek the benefit of the doubt. Not that <b>Derek</b> was without flaws, I mean somebody teach the guy how to smile, seriously Derek, you can smile for free! Just turn the corner of your mouth up, almost no effort at all. Try it. But still, in the Derek vs. Webster situation, you could spot from a MILE AWAY who was the good guy and who wasn't. I mean from the second Webster appeared he just acted cocky and too-full-of-himself for me to have any doubts. And that fact just made Elise' attitude that much more unlikeable. Maybe if the author had written more intrigue, like if we the readers weren't able to tell who was trustworthy and who wasn't, <i>maybe then</i> we would be able to sympathize with Elise more. But the fact that I knew from the beginning and Elise kept being all like <i>"I'm better than everyone because I don't want to be friends with Derek and I choose the loner one"</i> just had me rolling my eyes so much it actually started to hurt and I had to stop and give my eyeballs a rest. The fact that Elise was so close minded to even consider anything outside her quest to be above the rest was exasperating.<br /><br />Of course, she eventually comes to the realization that she's wrong and gets a bit more likeable, but that's close to the end of the book. Derek also becomes more likeable once he spits out "Webster's mystery", which he should have said from the beginning, but whatever. And Webster, well... he gets a two-dimensional character with not depth at all. In the end, I was somewhat excited to see Elise and Derek together, I mean I did get this book for a fun guilty-pleasure romance after all, and they did have potential. Even if Elise had annoyed me the whole book and Derek had basically been given no development as a character, I kind of liked the idea of them together. Yet when it's about to get better the book suddenly ends. So abruptly in fact that I considered the possibility that I had gotten a bad version and was missing the last pages or something. <br /><br />Apart from Elise and Derek getting together <i>(come on that's not a spoiler, we all knew it)</i> <u>nothing</u> gets resolved. I mean nothing. The book actually spends more time dealing with issues such as the family conflicts, the Webster thing, etc. than the Derek&amp;Elise romance, at least from my point of view, and yet in the end when they get together none of the other stuff is even addressed. <br /><br />For example, <b>
  <u>the family dynamics</u>
</b>. First there's Layla's strained relationship with her family. Even though she was a bit annoying, I felt really bad for her, she kept being excluded from everything and of course it was going to make her mad and had her acting out. There was no satisfying conclusion to this, I was hoping for maybe one last sister-bonding or something where they show her that they don't exclude her from <i>everything</i>, or some character growth for Layla, or something... but no. Also their parents and their rules proved a bit too much at some points. Seriously what was up with all of them going to greet whoever was at the door TOGETHER as a big group all the time? Couldn't one person go alone? If I ever rang the doorbell to someone's home and I was greeted by six <s>creepy</s> smiling faces I would just run the other way. On that note, when Derek mentions this to Elise, saying her family is a bit intense, SHE FREAKS OUT AND GET MAD AT HIM. WTF? I mean Elise your family <i>is</i> intense, embrace it. It's not like he was insulting them, just pointing out the obvious, a fact which Elise had also pointed out on numerous occasions by the way. I mean Elise is sixteen years old and isn't allowed to wear make-up! I'm not a huge make-up fan myself but give them the choice <i>gosh</i>. And get this, they all can have cellphones but <b>they can't use them inside the house</b>. Not even a text message. OK. None of these family issues were ever addressed, there was never some development to this, or the their dynamic, which would have been interesting to read. But no, like most of the book, it stayed in its comfortable two dimension. On top of that, the mom's attitude towards Derek's famous parents was creepy to say the least. Seriously, she is a grown woman, what was she doing getting all fan-girly at a pseudo-celebrity! <i>(Cause he wasn't famous you know, his parents were. Someone tell the mom that)</i>. Her whole attitude was just plain strange, not even a little bit professional, and I found it very hard to believe considering she was the <u>principal of his school</u>. <br /><br />Moving on, then there's <b>the Webster thing</b>. The guy was going around seducing younger girls to take advantage of their rich families and he never gets into any trouble for it. <u>Nothing comes of it.</u> In the end it was just a plot device to have some drama between Elise and Derek, *sigh*. Still the author brought up a <b>serious issue</b> like this and, once her characters got together, forgot about it. It would have been much more exciting to see Elise and Derek team up to make sure he stopped taking advantage of younger girls for his own benefits, or something along those lines. At least some kind of conclusion, Elise's mother is <u>the freakin principal</u>, DO SOMETHING ABOUT THIS. Again nothing.<br /><br />So much of the story revolves around Juliana and Chase yet there is no substance there. We are told they like each other from the beginning and that's it. I know it's Elise's story but seeing as they are always together maybe we could have gotten to see some interactions more often, but no. The one conflict between Juliana and Chase is pretty moronic and made no sense. I mean it seems like Chase would have told Julianna he wasn't taking his cellphone seeing as he knew it was forbidden. And then if they were normal people they would have talked about it rationally once they were back instead of avoiding each other for reasons NEITHER OF THEM UNDERSTOOD. Plus Chase's sister, the reason behind the cellphone conflict, is just another two-dimensional character to add to the list, not to mention a huge cliché.<br /><br />So in conclusion, I didn't really enjoy this book at all. The characters were flat, not one of them was well-developed or given much depth at all. I really didn't like any of them enough to care about what happened in the book. Also, I feel like there were too many issues introduced and yet most of it got forgotten along the way. If the book had just focused on the romantic aspect, on developing a nice relationship with interesting characters then I probably would have liked it better. Instead of developing the characters, the author favored the inclusion of several issues that just served as conflict to further things along, and when the main characters go together forgot to give them any kind of resolution. I'd rather the book focused on ONE thing and develop it more thoroughly than have several plots opened and never go too deeply into any of them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="785658099474116488" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17834762970495814225">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Cute.<br/>Not mind-blowing, but it was a really <i>cute</i> young adult retelling of Austin's <b>Pride and Prejudice</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449067256ra/17229895.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Dereck's (<i>Darcy</i>) parents are famous Hollywood actors, and he's learned to be cautious around people.<br/><i>Naturally, he comes off looking snobby...</i><br/>Elise's (<i>Elizabeth</i>) mother is the new prep-school principal, and her father is a teacher. <br/><i>Both are embarrassingly strict/wacky...</i><br/><br/>The plot sticks relatively close to P&P, but it still goes off on its own here and there. Only one sister is missing (b</span>
  <span id="freeText17834762970495814225" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><br>Cute.<br>Not mind-blowing, but it was a really <i>cute</i> young adult retelling of Austin's <b>Pride and Prejudice</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449067256ra/17229895.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dereck's (<i>Darcy</i>) parents are famous Hollywood actors, and he's learned to be cautious around people.<br><i>Naturally, he comes off looking snobby...</i><br>Elise's (<i>Elizabeth</i>) mother is the new prep-school principal, and her father is a teacher. <br><i>Both are embarrassingly strict/wacky...</i><br><br>The plot sticks relatively close to P&amp;P, but it still goes off on its own here and there. Only one sister is missing (but it was the boring preachy one, so who cares, right?), and the Wickham/Lydia thing played out a tad differently (but only a bit!). Overall, I thought this one stayed a bit truer to the original than another retelling I read last year, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/560687766" rel="nofollow noopener">Prom and Prejudice</a>, so I was pretty happy with that part. <br><br>I can't stress enough that this is <i>Brain Candy</i>, because if you go into it expecting anything other than a fluffy Beach Read, you're going to be sorely disappointed.<br>I was hoping for this book to be a nice distraction on a Sunday afternoon, and that was exactly what it was!<br></span>

  <span id="freeText15339942594333306808" style="display:none"><b>3 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527282408ra/25597522.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And yet..... =)<br><br>This was so adorable! It wasn't perfect, and honestly I think that it should have been longer...there was a lot more material the author could have worked with. Overall it was a fun read. I definitely recommend it if you are looking for a good P&amp;P retelling (that doesn't have zombies).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527282408ra/25597523.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>----------------<br><br>Pride and Prejudice set in high school?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527113517ra/25587151.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15339942594333306808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137490960?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137490960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18119876945788055138"><b><u>Rating clarification</u> : 1.5</b> <b>stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419195336ra/13009216.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>☂ <i>I didn't like that book. Some parts made me roll my eyes. Others made me cringe. Anyway, that's only my opinion and I can totally understand why readers might love it. No judgment here :)</i> ☂<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419200462i/13009686._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>- <b>The plot was predictable</b>. Highly, <i>highly</i> predictable. I know that's a retelling of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> but come on. That's annoying to guess everything before the characters, because you end up doubting their common sense. <i>Buuut</i> I'll come back to that. <br/><br/>And for those who'd te</span>
  <span id="freeText18119876945788055138" style="display:none"><b><u>Rating clarification</u> : 1.5</b> <b>stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419195336ra/13009216.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>☂ <i>I didn't like that book. Some parts made me roll my eyes. Others made me cringe. Anyway, that's only my opinion and I can totally understand why readers might love it. No judgment here :)</i> ☂<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419200462i/13009686._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- <b>The plot was predictable</b>. Highly, <i>highly</i> predictable. I know that's a retelling of <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> but come on. That's annoying to guess everything before the characters, because you end up doubting their common sense. <i>Buuut</i> I'll come back to that. <br><br>And for those who'd tell me that I mustn't expect something unpredictable when I read a YA contemporary romance, I'd answer that <i>1)</i> There <u>are</u> some pretty good contemporary YA out there, like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1044148910" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1030223702" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1027649457" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> <i>(but obviously that's only my opinion)</i> and <i>2)</i> Of course if the romance part is predictable I haven't <b>any</b> problem with it. <b>But the whole "who can we trust?" thing is only boring when the only person for whom that's not obvious is the main character.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1419200462i/13009687._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Epic Fail was the characterization.</b> → <i>Sorry about that, but I had to throw that joke, you know?</i><br><br><b>#1</b> <b>Elise was a moron</b>. A stupid moron. Seriously. She likes to think she's different from other teenagers who judge people by their parents but <b>she does the exact same thing.</b> Okay, I must admit that Derek doesn't help her here at first but come on, take Webster for example : that's pretty obvious he's hiding something from the beginning. Okay, maybe not <i>the very first time they met</i>, but when he begins to basically bitch about everyone and play with her forteen-years-old sister at lunch, I must admit I had like, <i>thousands</i> doubts. <br><br><b>#2</b> <b>Derek</b> was okay, I mean, the guy <i>is</i> cute. And bi-dimensional. And boring. OMG, he was <i>so. damn. boring</i> : the dude is a freakin smiley : basically he owns 2 facial expressions. He grins, he doesn't grin. <i>Annnd</i> he grins, he doesn't grin. <i>Then</i> he grins, he doesn't grin. <br>Well. You saw my point. But he was a cute little smiley, I give him that. <br><br><b>#3</b> <b>Chase and Juliana</b> were decent enough - oh, except the whole <i>love at first thing</i> nobody never explains. Duh. They just met and they're in looooove, what a pain in a ass I am to not understand! <br><br><b>#4</b> <b>Chelsea is a huge cliché</b> : Oh, welcome mean blond cheerleader. It's been a long time! Her character is simply bi-dimensional and some of her actions just not make any sense : <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I still don't understand why she tried to ruin Chase and Juliana's relationship. I'm not buying the <i>your mother grounded me</i> explanation. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>#5</b> <b>The mother</b> was so creepy dammit! How in the hell can she be the <i>school principal</i> and acting all fangirly with famous parents? <i>How</i>? All her interest in Elise and Derek possible relationship was creepy as hell. I swear I was freaking out at some point.<br><br>So. I'm pretty sure I made it clear I didn't like the characters so much. That's not what bothered me the most though. No. Here's what <b>made me want to throw my reader across the room</b> : the <b>ending</b>.<br><br>- <b>Nothing is resolved in the end</b> : <br>✘<u>Webster's issue</u> : I mean, the guy is, I sum up : hanging out with YOUNG teenagers, DRUGGING them, taking pictures in inappropriate situations when they're HIGH, because he wants to take advantage of their parents' celebrity and <b>he is never ever threatened</b> by, <i>I don't know</i>, maybe I'm a dumb one but do you guys have heard of something called POLICE? They're those guys in uniforms you're supposed to call when you see such behavior. <br>✘<u>Elise and Derek's relationship</u> : The fact almost everybody thinks Elise decided to go out with Derek because his parents were famous is a quite interesting issue to deal with - Too bad the book ended without any resolution.<br><br>However, <b>the writing was okay and I did laugh a few times</b>, that's why I rounded up my 1.5 to a 2. <i>And because I'm such in a good mood, being in Christmas vacations and all</i>. <br><br>PS : Oh, <b>what's the deal with the diet coke <i>not so subliminal</i> advertising?</b> Seriously. I almost expected to see a polar bear appearing at some point. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234849638" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15941270852186622724"><i> <b> I simply loved this book. Period. No More No less. :) </b> </i><br/><br/>Contrast to its title <i> Epic Fail </i>, this one is an<i> Epic Win! </i> for me. It's a great modern rendition of Pride and Prejudice that has kept its own identity separate from the old classic. Its a great re-imagined version or counterpart to the classic love story of the headstrong and opinionated Elizabeth Bennet and the intimidating, aloof,and handsome Mr. Darcy which was retold in a modern day setting of outrageous teens with the characters Eli</span>
  <span id="freeText15941270852186622724" style="display:none"><i> <b> I simply loved this book. Period. No More No less. :) </b> </i><br /><br />Contrast to its title <i> Epic Fail </i>, this one is an<i> Epic Win! </i> for me. It's a great modern rendition of Pride and Prejudice that has kept its own identity separate from the old classic. Its a great re-imagined version or counterpart to the classic love story of the headstrong and opinionated Elizabeth Bennet and the intimidating, aloof,and handsome Mr. Darcy which was retold in a modern day setting of outrageous teens with the characters Elise Benton and Derek Edwards.<br /><br />Though its just a retold story it seems to be a different one. A typical person who doesn't have a clue about the story of Pride and Prejudice would never think this is a retold story to that one. The author seems to bring out something new through the structure of Elizabeth and Mr. Darcy's life and that what makes me love it more. <br /><br />Its a typical <i> lovey-dovey </i> kind of read, Yes, but i really do enjoyed it. It was funny and sweet. The characters are well flourised. It consists of all the classic argues present to a typical high school relationships. It was a beautifully written novel and I can't really deny the fact that i do really love the story of Elizabeth and Mr. Darcy, its a simple one yet full of love, happiness and trials and as i've said often time <i> i'm a sucker for happy endings and stuffs :) So, yea. ♥</i></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9245686511233392228">Epic Fail... to me this book was an epic fail indeed. I did not like this book. The characters were boring. The storyline went all over the place. At time, I almost wished we could read more about Juliana and Chase because Elise and Derek were so boring. <br/><br/>There's just too many things I didn't like in this book. How the parents were so controling and old fashion. For example, the girls all have a cell phone but they can't use it at school or at home!?!? So I guess that gives them the ride back fro</span>
  <span id="freeText9245686511233392228" style="display:none">Epic Fail... to me this book was an epic fail indeed. I did not like this book. The characters were boring. The storyline went all over the place. At time, I almost wished we could read more about Juliana and Chase because Elise and Derek were so boring. <br /><br />There's just too many things I didn't like in this book. How the parents were so controling and old fashion. For example, the girls all have a cell phone but they can't use it at school or at home!?!? So I guess that gives them the ride back from school to use it? <br /><br />The thing is, there was potential. It could've been better if the parents didn't work at the school. If the girls weren't total goodie two shoes. If the ending was different...<br /><br />The ending: Really what was that about? I turn to the next page expecting more and I see : "About the author..." For a minute I was wondering if I'd skipped ahead without noticing (I'm on a Kindle). It just felt unfinish, but no it truly ended this way! <br /><br />I get that this was supposed to be a modern twist on Pride and Prejudice, but I have never read it. (GASP!!! I know... How could this be possible!!) So I have nothing to compare it too. All I know is that to my illiterate ;-) eyes, this story was missing something. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9245686511233392228" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1216176506" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216176506" />
    <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet"><img alt="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1387046887p2/13567836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1216176506?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘" href="/user/show/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet">Elise ✘ a.k.a Ryder&#39;s Pet ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11103008-epic-fail">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=3-stars">3-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13567836-elise-a-k-a-ryder-s-pet?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216176506" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18064265810930975456"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No one's family is normal. Normalcy is a lie invented by advertising agencies to make the rest of us feel inferior.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439538339i/15850376.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><u>*Might contain spoilers*</u><br/>What? How can you just end it like that? I felt like many chapters where missing and that we didn't get the full story, or the perfect ending... I mean, I felt like we only got the beginning of their relationship. Made me wish for a sequel.. However, it was a quick read and definitely not a waste of my time, which I actually was afraid it would</span>
  <span id="freeText18064265810930975456" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“No one's family is normal. Normalcy is a lie invented by advertising agencies to make the rest of us feel inferior.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439538339i/15850376.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><u>*Might contain spoilers*</u><br>What? How can you just end it like that? I felt like many chapters where missing and that we didn't get the full story, or the perfect ending... I mean, I felt like we only got the beginning of their relationship. Made me wish for a sequel.. However, it was a quick read and definitely not a waste of my time, which I actually was afraid it would be. I didn't even wanted to stop reading, but I had to because I could barely keep my eyes open, but as soon as I woke up, I went back to reading it :)!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I got lost in him, and it was the kind of lost that's exactly like being found.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The story was actually pretty awesome and adorable. I was a bit surprised at how much I adored it. It was funny as hell, with comments that I ended up laughing through the whole book. It was a bit...immature for me, since I love new adult and adult books more, but it was cute, easy and just what I needed at that time. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Basically, the world is a giant shithole. But some of us are capable of imagining something better.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br>Now the characters were quite cool, specially the heroine <b>Elise Benton </b>, mainly because she has my name (JK). I love Elise's comments, they were sarcastic, witty and funny. She was smart, not so shy, but still shy if you know what I mean. She's a great sister and a good friend. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He was tortured, brilliant, funny, gay . . . basically my dream guy.”<br>“Even the gay part?” he said with the ghost of a smile—which for all I knew was what passed for hysterical mirth with this guy.<br>“Especially the gay part,” I said. “I’m weird that way. “<br>“How’s that working out for you?”<br>“I’m beginning to think it’s not a good long-term romantic strategy.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Derek Edwards </b> was... weird, I think. I had difficulty to, I don't know, connect with him? I get why he is how he is, but still I wish we got to know him more. But he did have his moments and I did like him, but like I said, I wish we got more.. Derek was so...insecure? He was polite, yet cold and shut off. But we got to know him a bit better and he got a bit more confident specially when it came to the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kissing part <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Man, I hated not being able to figure someone out.<br>And from the slightly uncertain look he gave me as we all went to class, I suspected he felt the same way.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Now to the other characters.. <b>Juliana Benton</b> was cute and I loved the sister-bond she and Elise had. They did everything together, even Juliana's dates :P <b>Chase Baldwin</b> was super nice and a good guy for Juliana. They had insta-connection and guess they had the "love at first sight" thing, but since they weren't the main characters, it was alright and quite adorable :)<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You have a nickname, too?” he asked me.<br>“I could tell you, but then I’d have to shoot you,” I said apologetically.<br>He nudged Juliana’s elbow with his. “Will you tell me?”<br>“No way. She knows where I sleep.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Enter the people I disliked fiercely, <b>Layla Benton</b>, <b>Chelsea Baldwin</b> and later in the book, <b>Webster Grant</b>.. They were soooo fucking annoying that I wanted to slap them hard in the face. Specially Layla. I wanted to strangle her at some point. What is up with her?! She needs to get over herself and I almost feel sorry for Elise having her as a sister. Mean, I know, but damn you'd feel the same if you read this book.. Webster was pretty cool in the beginning, with his awesome and easy humor but then he turned creepy and disgusting and I'm glad Elise cut him loose. Chelsea was just plain annoying. Enough said. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Value people because of who they were deep down, not because of their names or their parents’ clout.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I got a bit disappointed in the end, and it kinda ruined the book a bit (or a lot, depends on how you look at it), I was a little undecided on what to rate it. So I just settled on....<br><b>Rate: 3.5/4 stars</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="18064265810930975456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156816647?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156816647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15335965430918752285">I have a love/hate relationship with retellings. On one hand I want it to be close enough to the original that I can see the parallelism. On the other I want it to be different enough that it's its own story. Because if I wanted to read the original, then I would just do that.<br/><br/>Given all that, I actually liked Epic Fail. <br/><br/>I liked how the author wasn't afraid to change stuff in order to give the story a contemporary feel. She axed one of the sisters, changed names and scenes... and I thought it work</span>
  <span id="freeText15335965430918752285" style="display:none">I have a love/hate relationship with retellings. On one hand I want it to be close enough to the original that I can see the parallelism. On the other I want it to be different enough that it's its own story. Because if I wanted to read the original, then I would just do that.<br><br>Given all that, I actually liked Epic Fail. <br><br>I liked how the author wasn't afraid to change stuff in order to give the story a contemporary feel. She axed one of the sisters, changed names and scenes... and I thought it worked! I particularly loved how she made <s>Lizzie</s> Elise's mother equally annoying and embarrassing while making her a modern working woman.<br><br>And the basic feel of P&amp;P is still there. You know... this: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422140937i/13461828._SY540_.jpg" width="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm not quite sure how the story will look like to someone who hasn't read P&amp;P before, but if you have then this will basically a nice and fluffy reminder. :)<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15335965430918752285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_314127124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314127124" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314127124?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=will-probably-regret">will-probably-regret</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314127124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16535627288977484717">This was a quick read, and fun, but suffered from trying to remake Pride and Prejudice. Seriously, unless you're <em>really good</em>, authors, don't do this! But what do I know? It's YA, so a little leeway might be extended. Still, that ruined some of the fun for me as a) it projected some plot developments too early (like knowing that the Wickham analog is a no good slime ball) and b) any deviations come across as weaknesses (deserved or not).<br/><br/>Take Caroline Bingley/Chelsea, for example. In this book, sh</span>
  <span id="freeText16535627288977484717" style="display:none">This was a quick read, and fun, but suffered from trying to remake Pride and Prejudice. Seriously, unless you're <em>really good</em>, authors, don't do this! But what do I know? It's YA, so a little leeway might be extended. Still, that ruined some of the fun for me as a) it projected some plot developments too early (like knowing that the Wickham analog is a no good slime ball) and b) any deviations come across as weaknesses (deserved or not).<br /><br />Take Caroline Bingley/Chelsea, for example. In this book, she's a conniving bitch actively working to undermine Jane/Julia's relationship with her brother because . . . uh . . . well, mainly because that seems to be the only way LaZebnik could produce the falling out from the original given that they were in High School and you couldn't very well have Darcy pull Bingley away on business and keep him away, could you?<br /><br />Indeed, the whole parallel falls rather dramatically apart around the half-way mark because of the difference between wealthy English gentlemen and High School students. I mean, you can't really have the guys called out of town, or have Lydia ruining herself and coming back triumphant at having a man forced to marry her, or have Elizabeth visit Darcy's estate with her aunt and uncle while on a trip while he isn't there (only then he is) . . . you see the difficulty. This is why it's so much easier to adapt Emma to a High School setting as all the action is local to a single neighborhood and all the players are present the entire story (at least, mostly).<br /><br />So yeah, not an impressive adaptation, I'm afraid. It was a quixotic undertaking to begin with and the compromises were too frequent and too intrusive to feel like it was adequately done. And I <em>really</em> resented having the reveal on Webster/Wickham so early.<br /><br />Which is too bad because the actual romance is touchingly well done and I liked the characters very well all on their own. I kind of wish LaZebnik had ripped these characters completely from their Austen origins and let the story flow on its own. All she really had to do was remove the Webster/Wickham thread, tone down Chelsea a bit (or ramp her up with motivations that made more sense) and create a reasonable conflict elsewhere in the school (it's a High School full of celebrity children, that's <em>teeming</em> with juicy, juicy conflict that any author should be able to mine for golden story nuggets).<br /><br />As it stands, it was a fun-enough story as a straight-up YA romance. It may have made a higher rating if it hadn't voluntarily jumped into the big leagues by leaning so obviously on Jane Austen, but sadly, we'll never know...</span>
  <a data-text-id="16535627288977484717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_180817364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/180817364" />
    <a title="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral"><img alt="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556432497p2/180315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/180817364?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral" href="/user/show/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral">Sophie Riggsby / allthingsequilateral</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/180315-sophie-riggsby-allthingsequilateral?shelf=adorable-quotient-is-high">adorable-quotient-is-high</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180817364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer257552938330239611"><i> *published on Mundie Moms on July 10, 2011*</i><br/><br/>Who doesn't love a romance story in the summertime? Well, I obviously do and any story that keeps the structure of my beloved <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> is definitely worth the perusal.<br/><br/>Claire LaZebnick brings the rhythm of <i>Pride and Prejudice's </i>plot into the modern day setting of Coral Tree Prep School in Los Angeles. Imagine a school where every kid is not only privileged but also related to a movie star or someone famous. Then imagine a more academic family</span>
  <span id="freeText257552938330239611" style="display:none"><i> *published on Mundie Moms on July 10, 2011*</i><br /><br />Who doesn't love a romance story in the summertime? Well, I obviously do and any story that keeps the structure of my beloved <i>Pride and Prejudice</i> is definitely worth the perusal.<br /><br />Claire LaZebnick brings the rhythm of <i>Pride and Prejudice's </i>plot into the modern day setting of Coral Tree Prep School in Los Angeles. Imagine a school where every kid is not only privileged but also related to a movie star or someone famous. Then imagine a more academic family moving from snowy Massachusetts to sunny L.A. because of their parent's jobs. What if that family consisted of four daughters, and contained the new principal of Coral Tree as well as a new teacher there? Okay, now you are all with me.<br /><br /><i>Epic Fail </i>is told from Elise Benton's point-of-view. She's the second oldest daughter and the one who is partnered up with Coral Tree's resident hottie, Derek Edwards. They are brought together only because Elise's older sister has fallen for Derek's best friend and sisters tend to stick together. You can already tell that I loved that sibling bond part, right? Well, I did. But, my heart went out to Elise as the moments of awkwardness and misunderstanding grew between her and Derek. Yes, I've read <i>P&amp;P </i>dozens of times and yes, I fall for the plot's high and lows every time. This adaptation had them all but tweaked them just enough to keep me interested.<br /><br />If you are looking for a smart, funny romance be sure to pick up <i>Epic Fail </i>when it comes out in a few weeks. As for me, well, I have to do something about that dreamy look in my eye that manifested itself after I turned the last page. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="257552938330239611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_163727417" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163727417" />
    <a title="Penelope" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/675363-penelope"><img alt="Penelope" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568151251p2/675363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163727417?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penelope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penelope" href="/user/show/675363-penelope">Penelope</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/675363-penelope?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163727417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2908234860275777474">It hurts to write this review, because I was so excited for this book. I love everything Jane Austen, and when I read modern versions of Pride and Prejudice, it just makes my heart happy.<br/><br/>Sadly, this one didn't quite do the trick for me.<br/><br/>While the characters were supposed to be modern versions of Jane Austen's characters, most of their personalities were too different. Elise (Lizzy's modern counterpart) began the story as a girl unsure of herself who let herself be bullied around by two other char</span>
  <span id="freeText2908234860275777474" style="display:none">It hurts to write this review, because I was so excited for this book. I love everything Jane Austen, and when I read modern versions of Pride and Prejudice, it just makes my heart happy.<br /><br />Sadly, this one didn't quite do the trick for me.<br /><br />While the characters were supposed to be modern versions of Jane Austen's characters, most of their personalities were too different. Elise (Lizzy's modern counterpart) began the story as a girl unsure of herself who let herself be bullied around by two other characters, and who even felt inferior when Derek (Mr. Darcy's counterpart) ignored her or brushed her off. Jane Austen's Lizzy would never have felt inferior in those situations! Later in the story Elise's personality starts to show and she is a much more interesting and funny character, but she is still full of self-doubt and has little sense of self worth...until she gets the guy. Yeah....<br /><br />The other characters were either flat, and showed hardly any personality beyond what we are told should be there, or were outright obnoxious. The romance between Chase and Juliana (Mr. Bingley and Jane) happens outside of the scenes in the book, so they seem to fall in love after just a few class periods. The romance between Elise and Derek starts out promising (he's very much like Mr. Darcy in the beginning), but quickly turns typical. Average, at best. Something about the story kept me reading all night long, so it's not without redeeming factors, but I still felt like something was missing.<br /><br />The good points of the book are the fantastic modern parallels to Jane Austen's day. Some of them were very clever and I applaud the author's ability to take what Jane Austen saw was wrong with the time period, and relate it to what is wrong in our time period, too. I also really liked the relationship between Elise and Juliana. They didn't get along perfectly, but they talked to each other and helped each other throughout the story.<br /><br />Overall, this is a very quick read that boasts some cute scenes with the main characters. If you think you will be able to keep this separate from Pride and Prejudice in your mind, you should definitely give it a try.<br /><br />This review was originally published on my blog. Read the full review at: <a href="http://thereadingfever.blogspot.com/2011/08/book-review-epic-fail-by-claire.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Reading Fever</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2908234860275777474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer613632095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2689959398793942155">I want to make an intelligent review about this book but I can't find anything else to say except that this book is... <b>CUTE</b>. Sort of.<br/><br/>It's the kind of book you read without having to think much about it. It's entertaining and if you've read Pride and Prejudice, then you can pretty much get the gist of the story.<br/><br/>There is nothing spectacular here and I find the writing too juvenile, which, I conclude isn't really a bad thing because it's obviously marketed towards the younger audience. I cannot rea</span>
  <span id="freeText2689959398793942155" style="display:none">I want to make an intelligent review about this book but I can't find anything else to say except that this book is... <b>CUTE</b>. Sort of.<br /><br />It's the kind of book you read without having to think much about it. It's entertaining and if you've read Pride and Prejudice, then you can pretty much get the gist of the story.<br /><br />There is nothing spectacular here and I find the writing too juvenile, which, I conclude isn't really a bad thing because it's obviously marketed towards the younger audience. I cannot really call it a "fail" book because I must admit I did enjoy reading this in a sort of this-is-silly-but-it's-cute-so-f*ck-it kind of way. <br /><br />I like the main protagonist, <b>Elise</b>, because she's a witty narrator though very self-righteous at times. I also like <b>Derek</b> because he's cute. Don't expect to read complex characters here and thought provoking scenes. This book is just pure, mindless fun.<br /><br />My only complaint is that the ending felt rushed and it ended when the lovers are just starting to hit it off. I was kinda sad because I am a happily ever after kind of girl. It would be more awesome if there's an epilogue that says <b>Elise</b> and <b>Derek</b> got married 10 years later and had 3 kids and a dog, probably a German shepherd. You know, something like that?<br /><br />But over-all, it is a nice book. If you want a nice break from all the heavy drama books and wants a short and fun read with PG 13 romance then I recommend this book. </span>

<div id="review_3526614055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3526614055" />
    <a title="Aarushi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/111485136-aarushi"><img alt="Aarushi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605470787p2/111485136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3526614055?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aarushi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aarushi" href="/user/show/111485136-aarushi">Aarushi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3526614055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6977457182399513004">This book is a disgrace to the masterpiece that is Pride and Prejudice, and I haven't even gotten to read the book yet. I just know this book is BAD. <br/><br/>Epic Fail is a modern-day retelling of Pride and Prejudice, which initially brought about my interest. Please don't read this. It will ruin the ACTUAL BOOK for you. Epic Fail is cringy, unfunny really, and is a literal copy of Pride and Prejudice. Jane Austen would be ashamed. <br/><br/>I didn't mean to read this book right now. I have around 21 books checke</span>
  <span id="freeText6977457182399513004" style="display:none">This book is a disgrace to the masterpiece that is Pride and Prejudice, and I haven't even gotten to read the book yet. I just know this book is BAD. <br /><br />Epic Fail is a modern-day retelling of Pride and Prejudice, which initially brought about my interest. Please don't read this. It will ruin the ACTUAL BOOK for you. Epic Fail is cringy, unfunny really, and is a literal copy of Pride and Prejudice. Jane Austen would be ashamed. <br /><br />I didn't mean to read this book right now. I have around 21 books checked out of the library which I have to finish this month, and this ebook is not helping me out. It took me about 5 hours to read the whole thing, and despite how fast I read it, this book is not interesting. <br /><br />Epic Fail is, again, an EXACT COPY OF PRIDE AND PREJUDICE. All the plot points were completely copied into this book, the only change needed was to make it fit "modern day". Every single dang plot point. I kid you not. Plus, it's like LaZebnik just took the worst qualities of P&amp;P (which aren't that many in the first place) and stuffed it in here along with more bad qualities.<br /><br />Let's talk about the characters. I did not like Elise very much. I don't know why, but even her jokes were not very funny, let alone Percy Jackson/Jace Herondale funny. Drake (or was it Derek? that goes to show how bland he was) is your Mr. Darcy impersonator, and he wasn't good enough. Mr. Darcy is freaking amazing and basically everyone's ultimate book boyfriend and perfect. Derek is Bland with a capital B. In fact, all the characters were bland in this book. I didn't feel nothing for no one. I'm ashamed to say I liked Juliette and Chase. They were also Bland®, but out of all the characters, I would want to be their friend the most. Lastly, Layla was bratty and annoying. The original characters were just.... better. <br /><br />The author tried to include a real-life issue in this book, what with Webster being (spoilers!) a pervert, but it wasn't really deep or a main-enough issue, you know? It's the definition of a fluffy contemporary. <br /><br />Do me a favor, will ya? I know Epic Fail might sound interesting because it's a retelling of a classic, but just read or reread Pride and Prejudice because you would be better off than reading this dumpster fire.<br /><br />At one point of my life, I probably would have liked this book. This is not that point of my life. <br /><br />2 stars :( I wanted to like this, I really did. I'm not gonna give up on the author, though. <br /><br /><br />You may be wondering that </span>
  <a data-text-id="6977457182399513004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5349426586581780393">A modern version "Pride and Prejudice".This is all I can say about.<br/><br/><br/>It was a fun read but there wasn't any mystery.After a first few chapters I had completely figured out the story,but the story- telling was good,so I kept on reading till I finished.Also I'm aiming for 100 books by 2011.So I can't leave any book unfinished :)<br/><br/>I love Jane Austen so Pride and Prejudice is also one of my favorites.But this constant retelling and reediting of her books is kind of boring and also not necessary.Whether </span>
  <span id="freeText5349426586581780393" style="display:none">A modern version "Pride and Prejudice".This is all I can say about.<br /><br /><br />It was a fun read but there wasn't any mystery.After a first few chapters I had completely figured out the story,but the story- telling was good,so I kept on reading till I finished.Also I'm aiming for 100 books by 2011.So I can't leave any book unfinished :)<br /><br />I love Jane Austen so Pride and Prejudice is also one of my favorites.But this constant retelling and reediting of her books is kind of boring and also not necessary.Whether it's a movie or book adaption of the story it's basically the same .I'm sure writers can do better that trying to make a statement by retelling another person's story.At the end everyone is going to remember the book only as another adaption of Pride and Prejudice. <br /><br />I don't want to discourage anyone from reading it.It was enjoyable,well except until towards the end.But I can't help comparing it to Pride and Prejudice.<br /><br />I think there could have been some more Elise &amp; Derek scenes,because there is only one or two parts that is completely about them being together and not Chase+Jules being around.Their relationship was not developed properly.And I'm still thinking why it's called "Epic Fail".But that is publisher's choice. <br /><br />Also I feel the story ended very abruptly.We get the idea towards the end that Webster Grant,got away with all his crimes.There should have been a bit of punishment for him.Then introducing Georgia at the end seemed pointless to me.She came to meet her brother saw Webster with another girl,most probably felt like an idiot and then left.<br /><br />But then at the end it's a fun and quick read.</span>

<div id="review_195985417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/195985417" />
    <a title="Namratha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114559-namratha"><img alt="Namratha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406702134p2/114559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/195985417?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Namratha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Namratha" href="/user/show/114559-namratha">Namratha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114559-namratha?shelf=jane-austen-revisited">jane-austen-revisited</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer195985417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12929765606602596055">-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br/><b>Elise Benton</b> = <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Bennet' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elizabeth Bennet</a><br/><b>Derek Edwards</b> = <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitzwilliam_Darcy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fitzwilliam Darcy</a><br/><b>Juliana Benton</b> = Jane Bennet<br/><b>Chase Baldwin</b> = Charles Bingley<br/><b>Webster Grant</b> = George Wickham <br/><b>
  <u>EPIC FAIL</u>
</b> = The Ya-Lit version of <b>PRIDE AND PREJUDICE</b><br/>-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br/>And that’s what the book is all about in a nutshell.<br/><br/>But being a die-hard <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pride_and_Prejudice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pride and Prejudice</a> fan means that I would like to ramble on for a bit</span>
  <span id="freeText12929765606602596055" style="display:none">-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><b>Elise Benton</b> = <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elizabeth_Bennet" rel="nofollow noopener">Elizabeth Bennet</a><br /><b>Derek Edwards</b> = <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitzwilliam_Darcy" rel="nofollow noopener">Fitzwilliam Darcy</a><br /><b>Juliana Benton</b> = Jane Bennet<br /><b>Chase Baldwin</b> = Charles Bingley<br /><b>Webster Grant</b> = George Wickham <br /><b>
  <u>EPIC FAIL</u>
</b> = The Ya-Lit version of <b>PRIDE AND PREJUDICE</b><br />-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br />And that’s what the book is all about in a nutshell.<br /><br />But being a die-hard <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pride_and_Prejudice" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a> fan means that I would like to ramble on for a bit.<br /><br /><b>Elise Benton</b> and her three sisters are the newest students at Coral Tree Prep, LA. The effluent school is littered with the rich, poutingly-perfect, privileged offspring of some of the country’s biggest and smallest celebrities. Coupled with the fact that Elise’s mother is the school’s new (<i>highly unpopular, slightly bizarre and extremely regimented</i>) principal, this means that the Benton sisters have a steep social-path to climb. Elise finds herself as a reluctant member of one of the most hallowed cliques in the school when Juliana catches the eye and admiration of <b>Derek Edwards’</b> affable best friend, Chase Baldwin.<br /><br />And who, pray tell, is Derek Edwards?<br /><br />Derek, with his sullen superstar good looks, is a God among the twittering demigods of Coral Tree Prep. He is the offspring of Hollywood’s most famous celebrity couple and is pretty much the uncrowned prince of the school. While Elise is not exactly immune to Derek’s rare smiles and flashes of warmth, neither is she floored by his snootiness and odd tendency to sometimes act like a Grad A Jerk. Instead, she prefers the sunnier charms of social outcast, <b>Webster Grant</b>.<br /><br />And lo and behold! The saga of Lizzy and Darcy comes alive in a new and revamped setting.<br />-------------------------------------------------------------------------<br /><br />Elizabeth Bennet is one of my all-time favourite fictional heroines. She was someone I aspired to be. In a time when other damsels were simpering and clucking and having fainting frenzies, Lizzie was the exception. Strong-willed, a tad opinionated, not prone to frills and fancies and yet... a simpatico young lady who was doused with wit and wisdom. Fitzwilliam Darcy is my eternal fictional crush. I never tire of the seemingly snobbish gentleman who yearned for the love of Lizzie despite his better and questionable judgement. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Epic Fail</u>
</b> did a brilliant job of modernising my favourite duo. Elise Benton was an intelligent heroine who never acted like a lovelorn loon. Derek Edwards was brooding Darcy brought to preppy life. The dialogue was quirky and smart and a throwback to the banter from <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0147800/" rel="nofollow noopener">’10 Things I Hate About You’</a>. The Benton family was the embarrassing coterie that we cringed over in the original story. And then ofcourse, we have the plot twists and the character follies that symbolize misplaced pride and unfounded prejudices. <br /><br />I judge the power of an engaging read by it’s ability to compel me to finish it at a fiendish pace. I was done with this book in half-a-day. It’s not a classic. It’s not perfect. It has a few pitfalls. And no, don’t go by it’s lack-lustre cover. <br />It’s a bendy, light-hearted summer read that does justice to the mother of all chick-lit books. <br /><br />In short (<i>and I know it’s hackneyed</i>), the book is an <b>EPIC WIN</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12929765606602596055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4417134685299354137" style="display:none">This was good but I will not rush to put it on my favorites list. Why you might ask. While this book was told to me to be clean and there were some spots that pushed the envelope. <div id="review_1175553599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175553599" />
    <a title="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee"><img alt="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375405176p2/19569054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175553599?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gertiebee * the little book bee *" href="/user/show/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee">Gertiebee * the little book bee *</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of heartwarming YA stories</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee?shelf=may-reads-2015">may-reads-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19569054-gertiebee-the-little-book-bee?shelf=btc-half-yrly">btc-half-yrly</a>
